==PAGE:1==
Optimization of bridge design for
long span bridges
Rolf Gedevad Hovmand
Kongens Lyngby 2017
==PAGE:2==
Technical University of Denmark
Department of Civil Engineering
Brovej, building 118,
2800 Kongens Lyngby, Denmark
Phone +45 4525 1700
byg@byg.dtu.dk
www.byg.dtu.dk
==PAGE:3==
Summary (English)
The aim of this thesis is to develop a principle optimization program that can
reduce the material consumption of orthotropic steel bridge deck. This is done
not only to lower the material usage, but also to try to increase of the span
length for bridges by lower the self-weight of the bridge.
The program will be developed using matlab, python, and abaqus. matlab
will be the managing program that will run the minimization algorithm that will
reduce the material consumption. abaqus will be used as a FE analysis program
that will perform analyses of constructions, and python is used to model the FE
models in abaqus.
The deck from the Izmit Bay Bridge will be used as reference for the FE models
of the optimization. The optimization of the bridge deck will be for a stiened
plate at the top of the bridge deck between two diaphragms.
To begin with, an optimization program is made for a cantilever beam with a
discontinuous cross-section at middle span. This is done to make a connection
between the three programs, and to show that it is possible to make an opti-
mization program using the three programs. Two optimizations for the beam
are performed. The rst optimization is to optimize the material distribution
for a constant volume of the beam and to nd the lowest possible deection of
the beam tip. The other optimization is to nd the smallest volume of the beam
given a constrain of a maximum deection of the beam tip. The results from
both optimizations showed compliance between analytical results and results
from abaqus. The analyzes showed that it was possible to make an optimiza-
tion program using the three programs.
After that, the plate from Izmit Bay Bridge was optimized for stability and
fatigue. Many simplications were made in the FE model of the bridge plate,
including supports, but also the geometry was changed from closed trapezoidal
stieners to open rib stieners. These changes changed the design properties,
but it was accepted as the optimization program should be principle for opti-
mization of long span bridge deck, and not necessarily the one from Izmit Bay
Bridge.
==PAGE:4==
ii
The results from the stability analysis showed that the design was optimized
both for the initial dimensions of the design and for the Izmit Bay Bridge deck
plate. On the other hand, the fatigue analysis showed that there were problems
with the stresses and the method of extracting the results. The problem wasn't
solve, but suggestions to how it could be solved was presented.
Finally, a combined optimization analysis was made for both stability and fa-
tigue.
The analysis showed that there were still problems with the fatigue
analysis, but also that the optimization program could solve two optimization
problems at the same time. The optimization program thus has the potential
to make optimizations of orthotropic bridge decks by improving the FE models
and the method of extracting data.
==PAGE:5==
Summary (Danish)
Målet for denne afhandling er at udvikle et principielt optimeringsprogram, som
kan reducere materialeforbruget for orthotrope stålbrodæk. Dette gøres, for at
muliggøre forøgelsen af spændlængden for broer.
Programmet vil blive udviklet vha. matlab, python og abaqus. matlab vil
være det styrende program, som vil køre minimerings algoritmen, der vil redu-
cere materialeforbruget. abaqus anvendes som analyse program, der vil udføre
analyser af konstruktioner, og python anvendes til at modellere FE modellerne
i abaqus.
Brodækket, der tages udgangspunkt i for optimerings FE modellerne, er fra bro-
en Izmit Bay Bridge. I optimeringsprogrammet ses der på en afstivede plade i
toppen af brodækket og som er placeret imellem to slidsevægge.
Til at starte med laves et optimeringsprogram for en udragende bjælke med dis-
kontinuerlig tværsnit på midten af bæjlken. Dette gøres for at oprette forbindelse
mellem de tre programmer, og for at vise, at det er muligt at lave et optime-
ringsprogram med de tre programmer. Der udføres to optimeringer for bjælken.
Den første optimering er, at optimere materialefordelingen ved konstant volu-
men af bjælken og nde den mindst mulige nedbøjning af bjælkeenden. Den
anden optimere er at nde det mindste volumen af bjælken givet en begræns-
ning iform af en maximal nedbøjning. Resultaterne viste, at det var muligt at
lave et optimeringsprogram vha. de tre programmer.
Herefter blev pladen fra Izmit Bay Bridge optimeret for stabilitet og udmattelse.
Der blev foretaget mange simpliceringer i FE modellen af bropladen heriblandt
understøttinger men også geometrien blev ændret fra lukkede trapezformede af-
stivere til åbne ribbe afstivere. Dette ændrede på konstruktionens egenskaber,
men det blev accepteret, da optimeringsprogrammet skulle være principielt for
broer med lang spænd og ikke nødvendigvis Izmit Bay Bridge.
Resultaterne fra stabilitetsanalysen viste, at konstruktionen blev optimeret bå-
de mht. startdimensionerne for konstruktionen og mht. pladen fra Izmit Bay
Bridge. Derimod viste analysen for udmattelse, at der var problemer med spæn-
dingerne og den måde resultaterne blev trukket ud på. Problemet blev ikke løst,
==PAGE:6==
iv
men der blev givet forslag til hvordan det kunne løses.
Til sidst blev en samlet optimeringsanalyse foretaget for både stabilitet og ud-
mattelse. Analysen viste, at der fortsat var problemer udmattelsesundersøgel-
sen, men også, at optimeringsprogrammet kunne løse to optimeringsproblemer
på samme tid. Optimeringsprogrammet har dermed potentiale til at kunne fo-
retage optimeringer af orthotrope brodæk ved forbedrelse af FE modellerne og
udtrækningen af data.
==PAGE:7==
Preface
This thesis was prepared at the department of Civil Engineering at DTU in
fullment of the requirements for acquiring an M.Sc. in Civil Engineering.
The thesis deals with optimization of bridge deck for long span bridges, by
developing an optimization program using the programs matlab, python and
abaqus.
The thesis has been prepared in a period from 2nd of January to the 8th July,
and it is representing 32.5 ECTS points.
Lyngby, 8. July2017
Rolf Gedevad Hovmand

Chapter 1
Introduction
In modern bridge design, the orthotropic steel deck rib system has become more
popular ever since it was invented by German engineers in the 1950s [18]. This
is due to the light weight and high stiness. The orthotropic steel decks have
made it possible to make more slender bridges and increase the span lengths.
For instance is the orthotropic steel deck system used in the Japanese suspen-
sion bridge Akashi Kaiky	o Bridge, which has the longest span in the world.
Also the Great Belt Bridge in Denmark is build using orthotropic steel decks.
The name orthotropic comes from the words orthogonal and anisotropic. In
general the bridge deck system consist of a steel plate, which are stiened lon-
gitudinally or transversely, or both directions. This gives anisotropic structural
properties orthogonally in the bridge deck, which is the reason to the name.
The rib system can be open or closed. An overview of the dierent rib systems
are shown in Figure 1.1.
Figure 1.1: (Left) Open and (Right) closed rib systems.[1]
==PAGE:16==
2
Introduction
The rib system is used in many types of bridges (Plate-Girder bridges, Box-
Girder bridges, Movable bridges, Truss bridges, Cable-Stayed bridges and Sus-
pension bridges) [18]. The systems have been improved though the years, but
the optimal rib system is depending on the individual bridge, due to dierent
load cases for each bridge. However, from experiments it has been found that
the most practical rib system is a closed rib system with a trapezoidal shape
[18]. This is also the type that is used for the bridges with the longest main
span.
When designing orthotropic steel decks, aspects like stress distribution, stabil-
ity, deections and shear force distribution are considered, but it has turned
out that the most critical problem with the orthotropic decks is fatigue. For
the past decades investigations of fatigue failures have been performed, which
shows that most of the fatigue fails was cause by cracks. The fatigue cracks
occurred at the welded connection details, such as the rib-to-deck plate and
rib-to-diaphragm, because the connections are sensitive to large stresses and
residual stresses, which occur because of the self-weight and wheel load [5]. It
is therefore important to take fatigue into account when designing orthotropic
bridges since this is the limiting factor for the lifetime of the bridge.
Figure 1.2: Rib-to-deck plate cracks. [27]
Construction of a bridge is very expensive. As an example, in the period from
1990-1998 the Danish government paid 24.1 billion DKK for the Great Belt
Bridge. If the bridge was build in 2017, the price would be DKK 33.8 billion
which corresponds to USD 5.1 billion see Appendix A. If the bridge deck was
optimized in order to reduce the material usage, the self-weight and the resource
cost of the bridge would also be reduced. This would be benecial nancially
and for the nature. Furthermore, the reduction of the self-weight would make
it possible to increase the main span of bridges, due to the lower self-weight of
the bridge.
The purpose of this project is to develop a nite element (FE) optimization pro-
==PAGE:17==
3
gram that can nd the optimal dimensions of the components in an orthotropic
steel deck in order to get the lowest possible volume. The Izmit Bay Bridge see
chapter 3, is used as a reference bridge, since it will be one of the most optimized
orthotropic bridge decks and have one of the longest main span in the world.
The bridge has a record of 5m between the diaphragms, where the Great Belt
Bridge has 4m between the diaphragms. This however leads to a larger stiness
requirement of the orthotropic deck.
The program that will handle the optimization algorithm is matlab and the
FE program used for the structural analysis is the commercial program abaqus.
First a simple cantilever beam is optimized. This optimization is performed to
show that it is possible to make an optimization program using matlab's built-
in algorithm and abaqus as structural analyzer. When it is shown that the
optimization is possible using the programs, the bridge deck will be analyzed
for stability and fatigue. The FE model of a full bridge deck is a complicated
model consisting of beam, plate and shell elements. The optimization program
is therefore developed for a single top lane plate between to diaphragms. This is
done to make a more simple model and to make small steps toward developing
a optimization program for a full scale bridge deck.
Even though the basis of the FE model is the Izmit Bay Bridge, the geometry
of the rib system is changed from a closed trapezoidal rib system to a open
vertical plated system in FE model. This is done to simplify the geometry of
the model. An optimization program for both stability and fatigue is developed
though out the report for the FE model, and nally a combined optimization
of the FE model will be performed.
==PAGE:18==
4
Introduction
==PAGE:19==
Chapter 2
Background study
Since the orthotropic steel deck was invented in the 1950s a lot of research of the
deck have been made. Before starting the project, a literature study was made
to see if a similar project, where an optimization program for an orthotropic
steel deck was developed by using matlab, python and abaqus.
The study quickly showed that the primarily research for the orthotropic bridge
deck was to optimize the bridges for fatigue cracks. This was due to reports of
fatigue cracks in a large number of bridges all over the world [4] [5] [6]. Ever since
the fatigue cracks were detected, large eorts have been made to prevent the
fatigue cracks. In the 90's, lots of research were conducted for the Eurocodes,
which developed guidelines and categorized the specic detail fatigue cracks into
fatigue categories [7]. The guidelines and fatigue categories is also known as the
nominal stress approach, and it is the most commonly used fatigue verication
[6] [8] [9].
In order to prevent the fatigue cracks many parametric studies of changing the
thicknesses of the dierent members have been made [8] [9] [10] [11] [12] [13] [14].
Typically the parameters studied was the the thickness of the top plate and the
thickness of the ribs. Most of the results showed that increasing the deck plate
will reduce the considered stress range, and that the optimal dimension for the
bridge deck was individual for each specic bridge.
==PAGE:20==
6
Background study
Further investigation to nd new concepts of an orthotropic deck, where fatigue
cracks do not appear, is still ongoing. This shows that the primarily focus on
optimizing the orthotropic bridges has been on nd a new design concept for the
rib system, and not to make a program, which can nd the optimal dimensions
for members of the bridge deck based on known concepts.
This project is not about nding new calculation methods for fatigue cracks or to
come up with new concepts for rib systems and investigate themes. The project
is to use a current rib system and to use the already known design concepts,
such as the nominal stress approach presented by the Eurocode, to optimize the
bridge deck with respect to the material usage. Based on the literature study,
this has not been made before, or atleast not with the procedure used in this
project.
When the members in the bridge deck are pushed to their geometrical limits, the
phenomena buckling can occur in the members [22]. Therefore, two structural
analyzes are performed in the optimization program for the bridge deck: one
for stability of the structural members and one for fatigue cracks.
==PAGE:21==
Chapter 3
Izmit Bay Bridge
Throughout this project an optimization program for optimizing orhtotropic
steel decks is developed. As an basis for the development of the program, the
Izmit Bay Bridge (IBB) is used. The bridge is located at the Gulf of Izmit at
the eastern end of the Sea of Marmara and approximately 50 km south-east of
Istanbul. The bridge is also known as the Osman Gazi Bridge, and it is the
largest part of the Osman Gazi project. Besides the IBB the project consist of
420 km highway. The project aimed to improve the Turkish infrastructure and
industry by reducing the travel time from Izmir to the city of Istanbul. The
project was completed 30. of June 2016, it costed US$ 1.2 billion and the travel
time was reduced from six-and-half hours to three-and-half hour between the
two cities. [22]
The IBB was designed by the Japanese company IHI and the architectural
rm Dissing+Weitling. The engineering design was performed by the Danish
engineering company COWI A/S.
The bridge is a suspension bridge with a 1550 m main span (the fourth longest
in the world) and two side spans each 566 m long. In Figure 3.1 and Figure 3.2
the side-view of the entire bridge and a close-up on the southern part of the
bridge can be seen respectively. The geometry of the bridge in the gures are
for the nal state of the bridge, which means that the cables and hangers need
to be pre-tensioned in order to get the geometry due to the dead load. The
pre-tension of the cables will not be investigated in this project.
The girder and pylons are made of steel and the foundations and anchor blocks
are made of concrete.
==PAGE:22==
8
Izmit Bay Bridge
Figure 3.1: Side-view of Izmit Bay Bridge. [15]
Figure 3.2: Close-up on the southern part of Izmit Bay Bridge.[15]
The bridge has two main cables and a total of 202 hangers. The transverse
distance between the main cables are 30m. The main cables are anchored to
the anchor blocks at each end of the bridge and runs over the pylons in cable
saddles.
The girder of IBB is a box girder made of 25m long segments, which are as-
sembled midway between hangers. The bridge has six lanes, where the outer
lanes in each direction are designed to carry heavier trac. These lanes are
used as reference for the development of the optimization program throughout
the report. The geometry of the girder varies along the bridge, but a typical
cross-section of the girder is seen in Figure 3.4 and Figure 3.5. The width of the
typical cross-section between the pylons is 35.9m including inspection walkways
and the maximum height is 4.75m at the centreline (CL) [15].
==PAGE:23==
9
Figure 3.3: Typical cross-section of the girder.[23]
==PAGE:24==
10
Izmit Bay Bridge
Figure 3.4: Cross-section of the right side of the girder.[15]
The diaphragms, which are transferring the trac load out to the hangers and
gives the girder a high torsional stiness, are installed for every 5m in the longi-
tudinal direction. Furthermore inclined rods are installed in order to connect the
upper and lower diaphragm beams. The stiness in the longitudinal direction
is ensured by orthotropic trapezoidal steel plates (ribs) with a 600mm center
distance from each other. In Figure 3.5 a detailed cross-section of the girder and
the diaphragm are shown. The geometry of the ribs used at the outer trac
lane (reference lane) and the associated cut-out in the diaphragm are shown in
Figure 3.6 and Figure 3.7. Instead of the closed trapezoidal ribs the FE model
will be modelled with opened plate ribs. This is done to simplify the model.
The FE model is explain in details in section 7.2.
The bridge pylons are shown in Figure 3.8. The pylons are slightly inclined.
The pylon pair at each end of the midspan have the same geometry and are
connected by an upper and lower cross beam. The bridge girder is installed so
that only transverse support is ensured at the pylons.

(b) Diaphragm
and internal rods. [15]

Chapter 4
Programs and functions
To optimize the bridge to achieve as little material usage as possible the three
programs matlab, python and abaqus are used. The programming of the
optimization program will contain both self-programmed scripts and functions,
which are self written, and built-in functions, which are functions inside the
programs.
In this section the structure of the optimization program is outlined. It is rec-
ommended that the reader has a basic knowledge of the programs and that the
information in this chapter is taking into thought when reading the following
chapters. At this point in the report the content in this chapter can be hard
to follow. However, when looking at the scripts in Appendix B, Appendix C,
Appendix D, Appendix E Appendix F.
The optimization programs will have a general structure, however for each opti-
mization analysis the program will slightly dier. The dierences will be spec-
ied for the individual optimization analysis in chapter 7.
However, in this
section an overview of the general structure and the ow of data will be pre-
sented rst. A more detailed description of the scripts and functions written
and used in the analysis for the stability of the bridge deck is made. Finally a
description of the most essential build-in functions in the programmes will be
explained.
In chapter 7 the optimization programs will be used to perform optimizations
of structures to show that the program is working as intended.

Programs and functions
4.1
Program structure
To optimize the material usage for the orthotropic bridge deck the three pro-
grams matlab, python and abaqus are used. The idea of this section is to
give the reader an understanding of the basic programming without going to
much in details. It is however important to point out that it is expected that
the reader has a basic knowledge of the three programs.
The main program used to make the optimization is matlab. The main script of
the whole optimization program is called Main.m. The script will handle the in-
put data, such as dimensions, material properties, loads and initial guesses of the
variable dimensions for the structural analysis, and call both self-programmed
and built-in functions in matlab. Furthermore, the function that is optimized
(object function), which is the function of the volume of the structure, which is
analysed, is specied in Mian.m. A built-in minimization algorithm in matlab
eg. fminsearch or fmincon is performing the minimization. The minimization
function will call a self-programmed function Aba.m. This function writes the di-
mensions, material properties and loads to a python-le, Var.py. Furthermore,
it opens the FE program abaqus, and runs a python-le, Main.py, which is
containing the information of the structure and thereby models the structure in
abaqus. When abaqus has performed the structural analysis the script Out-
out.py is run and the desired results are written to a text-le, Output.txt. The
text-le is loaded into Aba.m, and the data is evaluated. If the object function
is minimized as much as possible and the potential constrains are satised, the
algorithm will stop and the results are send to the main script Main.m. If the
object function is not fully optimized, the algorithm will make a change in the
variable dimensions, and make the structural analysis in abaqus until the ob-
ject function is fully optimized.

overview of the dierent self-programmed les are listed in Table 4.1.

Built-in functions
Throughout the self-programmed scripts and functions some matlab built-in
functions are used. In the following, the most important built-in functions are
outlined.
fminsearch
In general the function is used to nd a minimum of a mathematical uncon-
strained function with multiple variables. In other words, the function is a non-
linear programming solver that searches for the minimum of a problem specied
by
min
x f(x)
where f(x) is a mathematical function that returns a scalar, and x is a vector
or a matrix. By specifying a starting vector x0, fminsearch attempts to return
a vector x, which is a local minimizer of the mathematical function near the
starting vector. The algorithm used for the minimization is the Nelder-Mead
simplex algorithm.
The algorithm is a so called heuristic technique which
means that it is not guaranteed to be the optimal or perfect method to use,
but it is sucient for immediate goal. The technique is practical to use, when
an optimal solution is impossible, because it can speed up the process to nd a
solution that is satisfying.
The fminsearch is called the following way:
[x, fval, exitag] = fminsearch(fun,x0)
where fun is the objective function, that is optimized, x0 is the starting point
of the optimization, x is the local minimum of the objective function, fval is the
function value and exitflag describes the exit condition, which can be found in
Table 4.2.
In this project the objective function fun is the function of the volume of the
structure denoted V in the main script. The output of the function x is contain-
ing the minimum dimensions, which is optimized for, and fval is the function
value (volume) at the given minimum point e.i. at x.
==PAGE:35==
4.2 MATLAB
21
fminsearch is used to nd the minimum height of a cantilever beam see subsec-
tion 7.1.3.
Table 4.2: Exitag and exit condition for fminsearch. [25]

Number of iterations exceeded options.MaxIter or number of
function evaluations exceeded options.MaxFunEvals.
-1
The algorithm was terminated by the output function.
fmincon
In general the function is used to nd a minimum of a mathematical constrained
function with multiple variables. Just like fminsearch, fmincon is a nonlinear
programming solver, which nds the minimum of a problem specied by
minx f(x) such that















c(x)
≤0
ceq(x)
= 0
A · x
≤b
Aeq · x
= beq
lb
≤x ≤ub
where A is a matrix for linear inequality constrained, b is a vector of linear
inequality constrained, Aeq is a matrix for linear equality constrained, beq is
a vector of linear equality constrained, c is an array of nonlinear inequality
constrains, ceq is an array of nonlinear equality constrains, lb is a vector of
lower bounds and ub is a vector of upper bounds. The nonlinear constrained (c
and ceq) are made in an separate self-programmed function e.g. aba.m, which
was explained earlier. The algorithm starts at a starting point specied in x0
and then tries to nd a minimizer for the objective function fun subjected to
one or more constrains.
fmincon has four dierent optimization algorithms. The algorithms are listed
below. The reason behind the selection of the algorithm is explained, but the
algorithms will not be explained in further detail.
• Interior point (default).
The algorithm can handle both large, sparse
problems as well as dense problems. The algorithm is strong because it
can recover form NaN and Inf results. Furthermore, the algorithm satisfy
the bounds for all iterations. It is a large-scale algorithm.
• Trust Region Reective. The algorithm is eective, but it requires a gra-
==PAGE:36==
22
Programs and functions
dient. Furthermore, it allows only bounds or linear equality, but not both.
If the requirements are met, the algorithm can handle both large sparse
and small dense problems eectively. It is a large-scale algorithm.
• SPQ. Just like the Interior point, SPQ can also recover form NaN and Inf
results and it also satisfy the bounds at every iteration, but it is not a
large-scale algorithm.
• Active set. The advantage of this algorithm is that it can take large steps,
which adds speed, and it is eective on some problems with nonsmooth
constraints, but it is not a large-scale algorithm.
A large-scale algorithm is an algorithm, that handles linear algebra without
the need to store nor operate on full matrices. This saves a lot of memory and
calculation time. In contrast a medium-scale algorithm creates full matrices and
uses dense linear algebra, which can use a lot of memory and may require long
calculation time. Note: a large algorithm can be used to solve a small problem,
i.e. the size of the algorithm has nothing to do with the size of the problem
and vice versa. The algorithm chosen is the Interior point algorithm, because
it is a large-scale algorithm, which will reduce the calculation time, and doesn't
need to be provided with a gradient. If the constraints are nonsmooth, which
can be the case for the optimization of buckling, the active set algorithm can be
considered. This is not done in this project, since the project is not focussing
on testing the built-in algorithm.
The function is called by
[x, fval, exitag] = fmincon(fun,x0,A,b,Aeq,beq,lb,ub,nonlcon,optimiotions)
The call to the function is similar to the one of fminsearch. It is important to
note, that all the inputs need to be specied if the nonlinear constrain function
(nonlcon) is used. If there is no linear constrains, the vectors and matrices has
to be empty, e.g. in matlab the matrix for linear inequality constrain is specify
by A = [ ]. fmincon has more exit conditions than fminsearch. The exitflag
and the exit conditions are listed in Table 4.3. The optimoptions is specifying
a set of options for the optimization. This is described in the following.
It is important to note, that fmincon is a gradient-based method, which is
designed to work on problems where the objective and constraint functions are
both continuous and have continuous rst derivatives.

program possible to work properly, because of the loss of digits in abaqus. This
is explained and discussed more detailed in section 4.5.

vantage of not using the GUI is that the analysis is performed more smooth and

system(['abaqus cae', mo, myscript])

out (mo = 'noGUI') the GUI, and myscript is the main python-script, that is

Built-in functions
The important built-in functions are outlined in the following.
waitForCompletion
When running the python script, all variables in the script is checked to see
if there are any unknowns, before the script is actually started. Because of this
procedure, the programme will make an error message, because it can't nd
the odb-le from abaqus, since abaqus hasn't started or ended its analysis.
By using the built-in function waitForCompletion after the job in abaqus
are submitted, it is possible for abaqus to perform the analysis and make the
output-le. After the analysis is done, the python-script continues whit the rest
of the script.
openOdb
The results from abaqus are stored as binary numbers in an odb-le. To access
the obd-le and to convert the results to readable numbers the function open-
Odb is used. The desired results can then be extracted and written to a txt-le.
It is important to remember to close the Odb-le again by using odb.close().
4.4
ABAQUS
abaqus is used to perform structural analyzes for the optimization problems.
For that reason no programming is performed in this program. Still some built-
in functions are used. These are explained in the following.
MPC-BEAM
MPC (Multi-Point Constraint) is a type of connection that denes multi-point
constraints between two points. This can be in form of linear and nonlinear
constrains between nodes. This is useful to connect two parts with dierent and
continuously changing cross-section throughout an analysis, e.g. an optimization
analysis.
The built-in type MPC-BEAM is establishing the connection between two nodes
by a rigid beam, which constrain the displacement and rotation at the rst node
==PAGE:41==
4.4 ABAQUS
27
to the displacement and rotation at the second node. This connector type is
used to connect two beam parts in section 7.1.
Tie
The tie connector ties two surfaces together for the duration of a simulation.
There are two types of surface-based tie formulations Surface-to-surface and
Node-to-surface. The Surface-to-surface formulation is used in this project to
transfer the load from the trucks wheels to the bridge deck. By using the Surface-
to-surface, a master and a slave surface has to be specied. For the optimization
of fatigue (see section 7.3), the truck wheels will be the slave surface and the
bridge will be the master surface. The tie connector constrains the nodes of
the slave surface to have the same motion as the closets node on the master
surface. Furthermore, it will take the initial thickness and oset of the shell
elements underlying the surface into account and it allows transitions in mesh
density within the model. This is every useful, since the elements in the model
are shells and the wheels and deck will have displaced mesh to each other.
==PAGE:42==
28
Programs and functions
4.5
Limitation of program
Before making an optimization program for the whole bridge deck, an optimiza-
tion for the displacement of a cantilever beam is performed, see section 7.1. The
performance of the optimization showed incorrect results between an analytical
solution and the one obtained from abaqus at the beginning. An investigation
was made to nd the reason for this. It turned out that abaqus uses some kind
of function like oat(6) when writing the input-le (inp-le) for the analysis.
This means that only six numbers are written to the input le even though
the value has more than 6 digits. As default fminsearch and fmincon have a
minimum change in variables for nite-dierence gradients (a positive scalar)
at 0, ie. that matlab can make a change in the variable down to 0. MAT-
LAB made a change of 10−15, which was too small of a change because of the
digit limitation of the input to the inp-le. It is important to point out, that
MATLAB uses absolute values for tolerances. To get around the problem, the
built-in function optimoptions was used, where diminchange was set to 10−5.
Thereby, it was possible to perform the analysis and get acceptable results as
shown in section 7.1. The limitation of the input data has a huge eect on the
results, as they can be rounded to rough, e.g if the dimensions in the analysis
are in meters, the result will only be certain for 10−5 as long as no dimension
is larger than 10 m.
The problem can be solved by writing the inp-le itself, but taking the time
into consideration, it was decided, that it would be too time consuming and
that there was a larger probability of making writing errors.
==PAGE:43==
Chapter 5
Stability
Stability is the phenomena where a physical system can return to equilibrium
when it is slightly disturbed.
When a structure is at its geometrical limits,
i.e. the structure becomes slender e.g. long slender struts, thin at plates or
thin cylindrical shells, instability can occur in the structure when compression
stresses exits. Looking at the column exposed to an axial compression force N in
Figure 5.1. The column is initially straight and is in equilibrium for small values
of N, which means that even though a disturbing force would cause deections,
the column would return to its straight position. When the compression force
reaches a certain level, the stable equilibrium reaches a limit. This level of the
load is called the critical load and is denoted Ncr. At this stage, also known
as the bifurcation point, the column is still in equilibrium, however if the
structure deects by a small disturbance, the deformations will be permanently.
If the load exceeds Ncr the straight positioning of the column will be unstable.
At this point a slight disturbance will cause large displacements and will lead to
a collapse of the column by buckling. In Figure 5.2 the deection relationship
compared to the axial force is shown.
Figure 5.1: Simple supported col-
umn. [22]
Figure 5.2: Axial force vs deec-
tion relationship. [22]
==PAGE:44==
30
Stability
If the structure is not perfectly straight at the beginning the deection already
starts when the load is applied. Therefore, no sudden buckling by bifurcation
occurs, however a continuous increase in the deection will happen.
In this
project, the structural members are assumed to be perfectly straight, and the
instability will occur when the load exceeds the critical load Ncr.
5.1
Buckling of plates
Buckling of a plate is on many point identical to the buckling of an idea column.
As long as the load doesn't exceed the critical load, both column and plate will
stay straight. The major dierence between the columns, plates and shells in the
elastic range is the bearing capacity. For the columns all the bearing capacity
is used when the critical load is reached, whereas the plate in the case where
the postcritical strength is achieved with acceptably small lateral deections
will have some bearing capacity left and a load greater than the critical load is
acceptable. This is illustrated in Figure 5.3.
Figure 5.3: Elastic postbuckling curves for compressed elements. [22]
The extra bearing capacity for the plate comes from the out-of-plane deections,
which occur when the plate tends to buckle and results in membrane forces
due to stretching in the mid-plane of the plate. This can be explained from
a rectangular plate as illustrated in Figure 5.4, where a single half-way buckle
==PAGE:45==
5.1 Buckling of plates
31
mode occurs. The plate is supported on all edges with either simple or clamped
supports and is subjected to an uniform uniaxial compression load. By changing
the plate to be represented as strips, it is seen that the longitudinal strips tend
to buckle. For a compression load larger than Ncr the strips will buckle, however
the strips close to the edges will be constrained to remain straight.
Figure 5.4: Fundamental case for compressive plate buckling. [22]
The buckling of the plate will cause an elongation of the transverse strips because
the longitudinal edges are restraining the movement in the transverse direction.
This restrain causes tensile membrane forces in the transverse strips, which will
apply a stabilising eect on the longitudinal strips.
This is the reason why
the plate has an extra bearing capacity after the Ncr. The ultimate load is
nally reached when the stiness of the plate has suciently deteriorated due
to material yielding [22].
Depending on how the plate is loaded, the buckle mode changes. If a plate
is subjected to more than one load component, the buckle mode can be an
interaction between the two load components. The dierent buckle modes are
shown in Figure 5.5.
==PAGE:46==
32
Stability
Figure 5.5: Buckling modes for plates. [22]
The number of buckles in the buckling mode depends on the ratio between the
length and width of the plate. If the length of the plate increases compared to
the width of the plate, the number of buckles increases. This is illustrated in
Figure 5.6 where k is the buckling coecient for axial compression and m is the
number of buckles.
Figure 5.6: Variations in buckled mode with aspect ratio for plate panel in
longitudinal compression. [21]
Though out the optimization process the ratio between the width and length
of the ribs are changing. This will cause the number of buckles in the ribs to
change, and will lead to local minimum points. It is therefore not certain that
==PAGE:47==
5.2 Stiened plates
33
the optimized dimensions are the global minimum point, which is the most
optimal, for the optimization.
5.2
Stiened plates
The desire to make longer and slender structures leads to an increased tendency
to employ thin-walled, plated structures. This is also the case for bridges. The
thin-walled plates are used to take in-plane force and are extremely exposed to
buckle because of their small thickness. An way to increase the stability of the
plates are to provide plates with open or torsionally rigid closed stieners. The
dierent stiener types can be seen in Figure 5.7. The stieners can both be in
the longitudinal and in the transverse direction. If the stieners are arranged
in a regular orthogonal grid, and the spacing is small enough to smear the
stieners to a continuum in the analysis, such a stiened plate is called an
orthogonal anisotropic plate or in short, an orthotropic plate [22].
Figure 5.7: (a) Open stiener. (b) Closed stiener. [22]
Even though the plate is stiened, buckling can still occur when the load exceeds
Ncr. Both the plate and the stiener can buckle. The stiener are more vulner-
able for buckling if they are opened than closed because of the torsional stiness
of the closed stieners. An illustration of a plate buckling between the stieners
and buckling of the stieners are shown i Figure 5.8. The plate can also buckle
as a whole. This is illustrated in Figure 5.9. These plates represent the whole
bridges deck, where the transverse stieners are illustrating the diaphragms. In
this project only one segment is analyzed, and the bridge deck is assumed to
be buckling as a stiened panel (c) in Figure 5.9, which is important to specify
when establishing the boundary conditions in the FE model.
==PAGE:48==

for ribs. [21]

5.3
Linear perturbation
In abaqus the buckling analysis will be performed by using linear perturbation.
For this analysis type there are only linear responses for each analysis step.
The buckling analysis is solved by using the eigenvalue problem to estimate
the critical (bifurcation) load for the structure. This is done by specifying an
incremental loading pattern, QN, in the buckling step. The incremental load
will be the compression force in the bridge deck. The magnitude of the load is
not important since it will be scaled by a load multiplier, λi, which is found in
the eigenvalue problem

==PAGE:51==
Chapter 6
Fatigue
Fatigue is the process of initiation and propagation of cracks though a structural
part. This is caused by repeatedly loading and unloading (cyclic loading), which
cause uctuation stress in the structure.
When the stresses reach a certain
magnitude, microscopic cracks begin to develop at the stress concentrations.
The signicant fatigue crack starts to initiate when slip in the plane starts.
This is caused by the dislocation movement, which serves as a stress raiser.
The dislocation movement is illustrated in Figure 6.1 as three dierent fracture
modes.
Figure 6.1: Three dierent fracture modes. (a) Opening mode (tensile stress).
(b) Sliding mode (in-plane shear stress). (c) Tearing mode (out-
of-plane shear stress).
==PAGE:52==
38
Fatigue
The fatigue process is typically described by three phases, which is illustrated
in Figure 6.2 and represented in the following.
Crack initiation phase: small microscopic cracks are initiated in the surface of
the material. The cracks are so small that they only extend over a few material
grains size. The cracks propagate in a slightly diagonal direction with respect
to the plane of the material surface.
Crack propagation phase: a dominant crack is developed and propagate normal
to the material surface. The crack growth at this stage can be described by
Paris' law.
Final fracture phase: the crack is so large that it can cause nal fracture in the
structure. This happens when the reduced cross-section becomes insucient to
carry the peak load without failure.
Figure 6.2: The fatigue process can be described by three phases; crack ini-
tiation (phase 1), crack propagation (phase 2) and nale fracture
(phase 3). [15]
Typically the cracks will occur at areas with high local tensile stresses, known as
stress raisers or hot spots. For steel structures the cracks are almost for certain
to propagate at the weld toe. The reason for this is that the welding process
imposes high tensile residual stress and discontinuities from where the crack
may grow. The discontinuities of the material decreases or remove the crack
initiation phase, which then allows the crack to propagate for most of its life
time. Furthermore, the weld causes sharp changes in material direction, which
increases the stress concentration.
==PAGE:53==
6.1 Local stress range
39
In order to determine the fatigue life time of a structure, the local stress ranges
are compared to an allowable stress range. Methods to calculate the local stress
range and the allowable stress range are presented in section 6.1 and section 6.2
respectively. The allowable stress range are determined by using detail classi-
cations and associated S-N curves.
6.1
Local stress range
The local stress range used for estimating the fatigue life time will be found
using a FE model. If the FE model is not made with a certain detailing level of
the welds, the stresses will be incomparable to the allowable stress range from
the detail category and the S-N curves. In order to make the stresses from the
FE model comparable three dierent denitions are used in general.
• Nominal or modied (local) nominal stress.
• Geometric (hot spot, structural) stress.
• Eective notch stress (notch stress, total stress)
Each of the denitions have limitations and place requirements on the FE model.
The dierences between the stress for the three denitions are illustrated in
Figure 6.3.
Figure 6.3: Stress distribution for welded attachments. [15]
==PAGE:54==
40
Fatigue
6.1.1
Nominal or modied (local) nominal stress
The nominal stress is the stress calculated in the sectional area under consid-
eration, that the local stress raising eects of the welded joint is disregarded,
but the stress raising eects of the macro-geometric shape of the component in
the area around the joint is included. Geometric features such as discontinuities
and misalignment can locally increase the stress. This can be taking into ac-
count by the use of appropriate stress concentration factors. These are used in
conjunction with the nominal stress to give the modied nominal stress in the
concerned area.
For a beam-like component, the calculations of the stress variation and the mod-
ied (also local) nominal stress can be done by simple beam theory, where the
eect of a welded on attachment is ignored. For the bridge the macro-geometric
eect is e.g. the cut-outs in the diaphragm beams, which is not included in this
project. Overall elastic behaviour is assumed.
6.1.2
Geometric (hot spot, structural) stress
The structural or geometric stress σHS is determined on the surface at the hot
spot.
It is including all stress raising eects of a structural detail, but it is
excluding the non-linear stress peak σnl caused by the notch of the welded toe.
The approach is generally used for plate, shell or tubular structures, and where
there is no clearly dened nominal stress due to complex geometry eects.
By using a FE analysis, the local stress at the hot spot will correspond to a
singular point in which the stress eld will not be exact, according to theory
of elasticity. Therefore, methods to approximate the hot spot stress have been
developed. One of these methods are the surface stress extrapolation method,
which is the method used in this project. The procedure of the method is in
accordance with IIW recommendations [17]. The linearization between the two
reference points is illustrated in Figure 6.4.
==PAGE:55==
6.1 Local stress range
41
Figure 6.4: Denition of hot
spot stress. [17]
Figure 6.5: Reference
points
of
mesh. [17]
High-order elements will be used for the FE model, which is explained in sec-
tion 7.2. The element length will therefore be equal to the thickness of the plate
at the hot spot. The evaluation of the stress will be at the mid-side points or
surface centres respectively, i.e. at two reference points 0.5t and 1.5t, as it is
illustrated in Figure 6.5 (b). The linear extrapolation is given by:
σHS = 1.50σ0.5t −0.50σ1.5t
(6.1)
6.1.3
Eective notch stress
In contrast to the nominal stress and the hot spot stress approach the eec-
tive notch stress is the total stress at the root of the notch, obtained assuming
linear-elastic behaviour.
This demands a very precise volumetric FE model,
which includes the geometry of the weld, in order to include the stresses from
the weld toe. The eective notch stress is compared to a single fatigue resis-
tance strength. It has to be noted that the stress range at the weld toe of the
attached structural members has to be assessed with the hot spot stress as well
as misalignments and discontinuities need to be explicitly modelled.
The method is useful for fatigue failures rising from the wield root and to com-
pare the eects of dierent weld geometries, but because of the detail level
required, the method is rarely used for practical purpose and not included in
the Eurocode [21].
==PAGE:56==
42
Fatigue
6.2
Structural verication method
The stress range determined from the FE model is used to assess the fatigue
damage done by the load. Since the scope of this project is to make a program
that can perform an optimization for fatigue and not to investigate the actual
fatigue damage, only one of many verication methods are used. The method
used to calculate the fatigue strength of the bridge deck is according to the
Eurocode 3.

detail categories. The categories for this project will be presented later. The
number of each category represents the reference value ∆σC and ∆τC for the

obtained for constant amplitude nominal stresses by:

6.2.2
S-N curves
As previously mentioned, the fatigue endurance, which is the life to failure
expressed in cycles under the action of a constant amplitude stress history, is
determined by using the S-N curves. The relation between the applied load or
state of stress needs to be related to the resistance of the structure relative to
fatigue crack growth, and this can be done by the S-N curves presented in the
Eurocode. The S-N curves are presented by a log-log-linear regression model.
The model is based on empirical test data, which relates the cycle nominal or
hot spot stress range to an endurance dened by number of cycles to failure.
The number of cycles are dened for a probability of failure of 5%. The S-N
curves for cycle nominal stress are shown in Figure 6.6.
Figure 6.6: The S-N curves dening the fatigue endurance as a function of a
nominal stress range. [21]
==PAGE:59==
6.3 Structural analysis for fatigue
45
6.3
Structural analysis for fatigue
In En 1993-1-9 Annex B the verication method for the fatigue resistance using
the geometric (hot spot) stress is presented. This would be in accordance to the
method used in the FE model. However, from Bjærre [15] it is stated that COWI
used the nominal detail categories presented in EN 1993-1-9 Annex A. There
were several reasons for this decision, but the most important is that Annex B
doesn't cover eects of misalignments. The misalignments from e.g. fabrication
have to be modelled an taken into consideration, however, this is every time
consuming, and therefore a more conservative choice using the nominal detail
categories were used in Bjærre [15] for the COWI design verication. This will
also be the procedure in this project.
When designing a bridge many construction details have to be investigated. This
has been done for the Izmit Bay Bridge by COWI. COWIs investigation resulted
in a damage report. The report results are adopted from [15] and are shown
in Appendix I. In this project the investigation will be performed for a plate
of the outer lane spanning between two diaphragms as explained in chapter 3.
Furthermore, the focus in this project is to establish a principle optimization
program and not to make a full analysis of the bridge. Therefore, is the detail,
which is experience the most fatigue damage, used for the optimization program.
The damage report is used to specify the detail. The detail is located at the weld
toe of the partial penetration weld between the orthotropic deck top plate and
the ribs. In the damage report, this detail is referred to as detail 1a. The detail
with the potential fatigue crack in the top plate is illustrated in Figure 6.7. The
nominal detail category corresponding to detail 1a is illustrated in Figure 6.8.
Figure 6.7: Detail 1a. Fatigue crack initiating at the plate underside caused
by transverse direct stresses. [15]
==PAGE:60==
46
Fatigue
Figure 6.8: Nominal stress category for detail 1a. [21]
The load for the fatigue analysis will also be simplify. In Eurocode 1 ve dierent
load models are accepted for evaluating fatigue. These models are called Fatigue
Load Model 1-5 (FLM). In the structural analysis for the optimization program
FLM 4 is used, since it is the most extensive model without using the recorded
trac data, which is not obtainable. Furthermore, FLM 4 was used for the
original design by COWI according to [15]. FLM 4 had 23 dierent vehicle types.
The dierent vehicle types are build up by ve dierent axle types. Each axle
consists of between two and six patch wheel loads, each measuring 320 × 220 mm
at pavement level. When designing a real bridge, all the vehicle combinations
has be investigated to nd the accumulated damage Dd. This is however too
time consuming, and therefore only the load with the most inuence will be
investigated. From COWIs damage report, it is seen that vehicle type 5A-H
Appendix I gives the largest damages for detail 1a. The geometric conguration
of vehicle 5A-H is illustrated in Figure 6.9. As it is seen from the gure, the
vehicle type consist of 5 axles: one steering and four standard, and the largest
load at the second axle with a magnitude of 100kN. Furthermore, it is seen that
the vehicle is longer then the distance between two diaphragms. This means,
that either the front part (axle type A and B) or the back part (axle type C,
D and E) is implemented in the FE model. It is decided that the front part is
used for in the FE model.
==PAGE:61==
6.3 Structural analysis for fatigue
47
Figure 6.9: Geometric conguration of vehicle 5A-H with load magnitudes.
[15]
The load from the vehicles are placed on the surface of the pavement. Because
of the pavement, the area where the load from the vehicles are acting is larger
in the orthotropic deck. According to Eurocode 1 [20] the dispersal through the
pavement and the orthotropic deck can be taken as a spread-to-depth ratio of
1 horizontally to 1 vertically down to the middle plane of the top plate. This
is illustrated in Figure 6.10. As the pavement is 60mm and the top plate has
a thickness of 14mm the dispersal allow an increase by 2 × 67mm of the length
and width of the load surface. For axle type 2 in Figure 6.9 the dispersal causes
an overlap of the two neighboring load surfaces. This is handle in the FE model
by making a simplication where the load is allowed to be distributed over a
single surface, which is representing both wheels.
Figure 6.10: Dispersal of concentrated loads through pavement and or-
thotropic decks. [20]
The placement of the load has a large inuence on the stresses in the bridge
deck. The worst placement of the load can be found using inuence lines, as it
is done in [15]. However, this will not be done in this project, but it has to be
investigated for a real-world design. The placement of the vehicle will be in
the middle of the lane.

Chapter 7
Optimisation programs
In this section optimization programs for displacement, stability and fatigue are
performed to show that is is possible to develop a optimization program for
orthtropic bridge decks.
The structure that is used for the optimization problem for displacement is a
cantilever beam. The cantilever beam will be optimized for two problems: the
rst problem will be to nd the lowest deection of the tip by having a constant
volume of the beam, and the second will be to nd the lowest volume for a
constant deection of the tip. The main purpose is to establish the connection
between the programs and to show that it is possible to use matlabs build-in
optimization algorithm to solve the dierent optimization problems.
For the optimization of stability and fatigue a model corresponding to the top
plate of the outer lane of the Izmit Bay Bridge is used. The plate will be stiened
with longitudinal opened plate ribs instead of the closed trapezoidal ribs. The
theory in chapter 5 and chapter 6 will be used in the optimization programs.
Each optimization problem and FE model is specied in the associated section.
==PAGE:64==

Optimisation programs
7.1
Optimisation for displacements
In this section two dierent optimization problems of a cantilever steel beam
with a rectangular cross-section are solved. The rst problem will be to nd
the optimal material distribution in order to get the lowest deection of the
beam. The second problem will be to nd the lowest amount of material used
for a giving maximal deection. The cantilever beam will be divide into two
parts each with a dierent cross-section height, which will cause a discontinuous
bending stiness of the beam. The part at the support is called Part 1 and
the exterior part is called Part 2. A sketch of the cantilever beam can be seen
in Figure 7.1.

7.1 Optimisation for displacements

7.1.1
FE model
For both of the optimization problems, a general FE model is used, where small
changes are made for each problem. These changes will be specied for each
problem. As explained in chapter 4 the FE model will be written in a python-
script and then applied to abaqus, which will perform a static analysis of the
cantilever beam.
The FE model of the cantilever beam will be a 2D planar deformable model,
where Part 1 and Part 2 will be modelled as an individual part each. The
material properties (Young's modulus) and the prole shape (rectangular) are
specied and assigned to each part. The properties are listed in Table 7.1. The
beam orientation, which is need to be specied, is chosen so that the underside
is at the bottom of the beam.
The two beam parts are connected with a MPC-BEAM connector, see section 4.4
for more information about the connector. A static step is created, where the
boundary condition and the load are applied to the model, see Figure 7.2. The
boundary condition is made in python by using the code xed, which means
that the displacements in x- and y-directions (ux and uy) and the rotation (ϕ)
are constrained.
Figure 7.2: FE model in abaqus.
The model is meshed. The element type used is B23, which are Euler-Bernoulli
elements, which disregard shear deformations.
The B23 element type corre-
sponds to the Bernoulli beam theory, which will be used for an analytical ap-
proach, in order to verify the results from abaqus. The mesh size has been
investigated to ensure converged results. This is presented in Appendix G. The
mesh is chosen to be 5 elements per part, see Figure 7.3.

keep a total volume of Vtot, i.e. the total volume of the beam will not change.

parts, it is necessary to establish an expression, where h2 is depending on h1 to
perform the optimization. From Equation 7.10 h2 is giving as
h2 = 2aht

(7.11)
In the follow both an analytical and numerical optimization of the beam will be
performed. The calculations for the displacement in the analytical and numeri-
cal approach will be based on the Bernoulli beam theory, which means that the
shear deformations are neglected and the beam has to be elastic. The analyti-
cal solution will be used to verify the results from the numerical solution. The
average height is set to h = 0.25, and the tip load is set to P = 1N. The model
and load is small compared to the size of a bridge, but as mentioned earlier
the purpose of this optimization problem is to establish a connection between
matlab and abaqus and to perform the optimization. The object function in
the minimization algorithm will be the displacement given in Equation 7.3 and
the displacement from the FE model.

7.2
Optimization for stability
Now that it is shown that it is possible to optimize a cantilever beam, a more
relevant optimization analysis for the bridge deck is performed. As explained in
chapter 3 the optimization will be made for the top plate with ribs for the outer
lane spanning between two diaphragms. This is indicated with a red circle in
Figure 7.14.
Figure 7.14: Cross-section of Izmit Bay Bridge. One of the outer lanes are
indicated with a red circle.
The geometry of the trapezoidal ribs, can be too complex to start with. There-
fore, a more simple geometry, where the closed trapezoidal ribs are changed to
open ribs, are used to begin with. The open ribs will be simple vertical plates
(see Figure 1.1 the one lowest of the open rib types). The placement of the
vertical rib plates will correspond to the places where the trapezoidal ribs are
attached to the top plate see Figure 7.15. The change of rib type will have
an inuence on how the bridge deck will perform. By changing from closed to
open ribs, the transverse stiness will lower signicantly, and the results from
the analysis will therefore dier from the results from COWI. Furthermore, the
inclination of the top plate is also neglected, to simplify the model even more.
This will also be accepted, since the optimization program will be a principle
optimization program to show, that it is possible to use the procedure used
throughout this project to make an optimization program of othotropic bridges.
Making this changes, the model will consist of a horizontal plate and 14 vertical
plate ribs. A sketch of the cross-section and the model in 3D is illustrated in
Figure 7.15 and Figure 7.16 respectively.

As explained in chapter 5 buckling occurs when a plate is exposed to compres-
sion. The bridge deck has a large internal moment primarily due to its massive
self-weight. The moment will not be investigated in this project, but a mag-
nitude of 109Nm is adopted from [15], since this was the moment used for the
test models in that project. The moment is split up into a force couple, tension
in the bottom and compression in the top of the bridge deck. The compression
force due to the moment will naturally cause a compression in the top plate.
==PAGE:79==
7.2 Optimization for stability
65
The compression force is determined by nding the elastic centre of the cross-
section.
Since the cross-section for the bridge deck is not symmetric in the
horizontally direction, the elastic centre needs to be determined. The elastic
centre was found to be 1.73m below the top surface. The compression force is
specied as a stress over the cross-section, and it is determined by Navier
σ = M
I ye
(7.14)
where M is the moment, I is the moment of inertia of the bridge deck and ye
is the distance from the top plate to the elastic centre. The compression force
was found to be P = 17.72 MN
m2 . The calculations of the compression force and
elastic centre can be found in Appendix J.
The optimization of the bridge deck will be to nd the smallest volume of the
plate by changing the thickness of the plate tp, the thickness of the ribs ts and
the height of the ribs hs in order for the plate to be stable. The permanent
dimensions of the model is listed in Table 7.7 and the material properties are
listed in Table 3.2.

In the following the modelling of the plate in abaqus are outlined.
7.2.1
FE model
The stiened plate in Figure 7.16 will be made as one single part in abaqus
with the given dimensions listed in Table 7.7. Since the plate and ribs have a
signicantly smaller thickness than the rest of the construction parts and the
fact that they are taken the compression force in their own plane, they are
considered as shells. The model is therefore made as a homogeneous shell with
prescribed shell thickness. The plate and ribs are each assigned a section with
their respective thickness and material properties (the material properties are
the same for the plate and ribs). Here the placement of the nodes in the thickness
of the shell are specied. It is important to place the nodes correctly, since the
load are placed in them and the results are likewise obtained from them. The
dierent placements of the nodes can be seen in Figure 7.17. Depending on
the analysis, the nodes can be placed dierently, but for the stability analysis,
the nodes will be placed in the middle surface, because the compression force
is distributed over the cross-section. If the nodes were not placed in the middle
surface, the compression force would make a moment/rotation of the plate due
to the eccentric placement of the load, which will have an inuence on the
buckling of the plate.
==PAGE:81==
7.2 Optimization for stability
67
Figure 7.17: Node placement in shell elements. [26]
The model is assembled and a linear perturbation buckling step is created for
the buckling analysis, see section 5.3. The boundary conditions are specied.
This can be done in many ways because it is unclear how exactly the deck
plates are interacting with each other. This means that if it is assumed that the
plate is xed supported by the diaphragms, the model will be too sti, but
if the diaphragms are assumed to be simple supports, the model will not have
enough stiness compared to the reality. The stiness of the supports will not
be investigated in this project. It is assumed that the diaphragms are simple
supports, because the energy needed for the plate to buckle is the lowest for
this type of supports see chapter 5. Furthermore, the deck can expand in the
longitudinal direction.
The same goes for the boundary conditions in the transverse direction. Here
the plate is connected to another plate. Depending on how the bridge deck is
buckling in the transverse direction, the boundaries of the model could be on
a buckle top, bot or at deck plane see the buckle modes in Figure 5.5. If the
boundary is at a buckle top or bot the rotation in the plane is zero, however
the boundary can move up and down. If the boundary is at the plane of the
deck, the boundary doesn't move vertical, but has a rotation. Furthermore, the
transverse boundary is considerate as a symmetry line, and the plate cannot
expand in the transverse direction. The eect of the two boundary condition
type in the transverse direction are briey investigated.
The compression load is applied over the whole cross-section. In Figure 7.18 the
model with boundary conditions and loads are shown.
==PAGE:82==
68
Optimisation programs
Figure 7.18: Boundary conditions
and loads for bound-
aries at buckle top.
Figure 7.19: Boundary conditions
and loads for bound-
aries at plate plane.
The model is meshed with the element type STRI65, which are 6-mode trian-
gular thin shell, using ve degrees of freedom per node. The elements are high
ordens elements, and the number of elements used in the height of the ribs can
be reduce, because of the 'midside' nodes.
There will not be performed a full investigation of the converging of the mesh.
Only in the longitudinal direction will a brief investigation be made. The con-
vergence investigation can be found in Appendix H. It was found that a mesh
size of L/20 was sucient. When designing in the real-world a full conver-
gence investigation has to be preformed. The mesh of the model can be seen in
Figure 7.20
Figure 7.20: Mesh of the plate.
All other settings than the ones specied are default. The scripts and functions

can be found in Appendix D.

Figure 7.22.
Figure 7.21: Buckling of the ribs. tp = 0.02, ts = 0.008 and hs = 0.5.
Figure 7.22: Buckling of the plate. tp = 0.02, ts = 0.02 and hs = 0.08.
The mode shape in Figure 7.21 shows that the ribs are buckling. This happens
when the ribs are long and thin, and thereby have a lower Ncr than the plate.
The other mode shape shown in Figure 7.22 shows that the whole plate is
buckling just like stiened panel buckling shown in Figure 5.9. This happen
when the ribs are short.
These two buckling types were also expected.
A
buckling type, which could have occurred but wasn't observed, was the plate
buckling in Figure 5.8 (a), where the plate is buckling between the ribs.

The result shows that the optimization program optimize the volume of the

From the gures and the tables, it is observed that the boundary conditions
have a inuence on the results. In general the dimensions are larger for the FE
model with constrain movement. This indicates that the structure is stier for
a constrain movement boundary condition. However, the deviation between the
results for the two boundary condition types, are very small. Furthermore, it
is observed that the optimization program show unstable behaviour, since the
optimized dimension are dierent for each initial guess. This could be indicating
that the algorithm fmincon is unstable. Still, even though the FE model changes
boundary conditions, the results are quite similar for each of the initial guesses,
which indicates, that there are some consistency of the algorithm.
A more
reasonable reason is the buckling coecient explained in chapter 5. If the critical
buckling load is determined based on the ribs, the number of buckles can changes
a lot when the height of the ribs are changed. Therefore, local minimum points
as indicated in Figure 5.6 can occur. If e.g. the ratio between the length of the
rib (L) and the height (hs) is 1 and 2, the algorithm could be nding one of these
points as a minimum point, which is actually a local minimum. It is therefore
important to make a qualied guess for the initial dimensions of the design to
avoid unintended local minimum points. The exitag 2 from the algorithm also
tells that the minimum is a local minimum, that satisfy the constrains.
Comparing the results from the optimization program and the dimensions from
Izmit Bay Bridge, see Figure 3.6. The dimensions from Izmit Bay Bridge is:
tp = 0.014m, ts = 0.008m and hs = 0.36m. From the optimization program the
dimensions are in the ranges: tp = 0.0081m −0.02m, ts = 0.0072m −0.00197m
and hs = 0.2372m −0.3334m. It is seen that each of the dimensions from the
bridge are in the range of the obtained results from the FE model except the
hs, which is slightly higher for the bridge. This is a very acceptable result when
the simplications of the FE model is taken into account, especially the change
==PAGE:86==
72
Optimisation programs
of geometry, since a lot of torsional stiness are lost by the change.
7.3
Optimization for fatigue
The last optimization of the bridge deck will be an optimization for fatigue. The
theory presented in chapter 6 will be used for the optimization analysis, however
because of time issues the stresses will not be found by the recommended ap-
proach for the geometric stress see section 6.1. Instead the stress will be taken
directly in the connection between the plate and the ribs. This is not ideal, but
it is accepted since the program is principle.
The structure for the optimization will be the same as the one used for the
optimization for stability. This means that the optimizing dimensions are the
plate thickness tp, the rib thickness ts and the rib height hs and the permanent
dimensions are given in Table 7.7. The optimization algorithm used is fmincon,
and the object function, input arguments and initial guesses are the same as in
Equation 7.15, Table 7.8 and Table 7.9 respectively. The nonlinear constrain
function is change to
∆σR ≥σHS
(7.17)
where ∆σR is the fatigue stress range and σHS is the hot spot stress from the
FE model.
7.3.1
FE model
The FE model used for the fatigue analysis is in general the same as the one
used for the stability analysis with constrain rotation. The geometry are the
same and the boundary conditions are the same.
For the fatigue analysis, a general static analysis is performed for the model
in order to nd the stresses in the model. Fatigue cracks typically develop in
the top plate form the welds. Since the welds are at the bottom of the plate,
the stresses of interest are at this place. Therefore, the nodes are placed at the
bottom of the thickness of the plate see Figure 7.17. The placement of the nodes
in the plate will not have the same inuence as it did for the stability analysis,
because the load is applied vertically on the plate from the vehicles as explained
in chapter 6. The load from the vehicle is implemented by making a structural
part for the vehicle and placing it on top of the top plate. The structural part
for the vehicle will be made as exible shell elements, i.e. the part has to be so
==PAGE:87==
7.3 Optimization for fatigue
73
exible, that it doesn't eect the result of the analysis from e.g. traction in the
surface. The two parts are connected by the connection type tie, see section 4.4.
The load and boundary conditions for the model is shown in Figure 7.27.
Figure 7.27: Load and boundary conditions.
The elements used in the model is triangle shell elements STRI65. It could be
argued that beam elements would be preferred for the analysis, since the load
is placed orthogonal on the plane of the plate. However, the shell element will
still be used. Furthermore, an investigation for the converging of the mesh has
not be done. This should have been performed. The mesh of the model can be
seen in Figure 7.22.
==PAGE:88==
74
Optimisation programs
Figure 7.28: Mesh of the plate.
All other settings than the ones specied are default. The scripts and functions
can be found in Appendix E.
Normally the stresses from the FE analysis are extracted by nding the stresses
at the integration points of the elements. When these are found, the stresses are
specied by take the average of the values in the integration points attached to
the node. Thereby are the stresses in each node found and the largest stresses
can be found. This would also be the preferred way of getting the stresses if
the material orientation would be the same for both the plate and the stieners.
In the model the plate will have one material orientation and the ribs will have
another, see Figure 7.29 and Figure 7.30. In the gures the cyan color is 1-axis,
the yellow color is 2-axis and the red color is 3-axis/shell normal.
Figure 7.29: Material orientation of plate.
==PAGE:89==
7.3 Optimization for fatigue
75
Figure 7.30: Material orientation of the ribs.
An attempt to change the material orientation so that the plate and stieners
would have the same orientation failed. abaqus came with the following error
message:The user dened normal of the material orientation of 8400 elements,
as dened in *ORIENTATION, is orthogonal to the GASKET, COHESIVE,
SHELL or MEMBRANE normal direction. Check input data. The elements
have been identied in element set ErrElemUserNormMatOrient.
Instead the stresses from the FE analysis were extracted from the odb-le by
using a macro. The macro takes the value from the nodes in the view port.
This implies that a stress plot for the structure has to be made in order to nd
the node with the largest stress magnitude. When the node is found, the stress
can be extracted from the list made from the macro. However, to be sure that
the node is at the same place in the model, the model has to be meshed with the
same number of nodes. For that purpose seeding the edges by number is eec-
tive, but it locks the meshing of the model, and it is therefore not the optimal
way of getting the values, however because of time issues, this was the procedure.
==PAGE:90==
76
Optimisation programs
7.3.2
Optimization results
Running the optimization program, an output of the stress distribution is shown
in Figure 7.31. Since the fatigue is caused by tensile stresses, the stresses in the
transverse direction (x-direction in the global coordinate system for the FE
model) is of interest. These are represented as S11 in abaqus for the plate. It
is important to investigate the material orientation of each part of the model,
because the orientation can dier from part to part.
Figure 7.31: Stress in x-direction S11 for the full plate. tp = 0.02, tp = 0.008
and hs = 0.5.
It is observed from Figure 7.31 that the hot spots are located at the back vehicles.
This was also expected because the load from the vehicles are larger at this
area. A close-up on the hot spot areas shows that the stress are largest at the
connections between the top plate and the ribs, which was expected as well.
The close-up is shown in Figure 7.32.
==PAGE:91==
7.3 Optimization for fatigue
77
Figure 7.32: Close-up on hot spots.
Using the constrain from Equation 7.17 the optimization algorithm stopped by
the lower bounds i.e.
tp = 0.006, ts = 0.006 and hs = 0.05.
This is not
the desired solution of the optimization analysis, but is actually a result that
is expected when looking at the stresses for the analysis step. For each step
in the analysis the corresponding hot spot stress, which was chosen based on
Figure 7.32, is plotted in Figure 7.33.
Figure 7.33: Stresses S11 in each analytical step.
==PAGE:92==
78
Optimisation programs
The gure shows that the constrain is satised at all times, and therefore is the
algorithm returning the lower bounds as the result. It is notable that for some
dimensions, the stress changes to a compression stress. This is unexpected and
could indicating that the model itself or the method of extracting the results
are incorrect. If a mesh control and a hand calculation was made for the model,
the results could have been checked. However, this is not done and the results
from the model are therefore questionable.
A small investigation is performed by making stress distribution plots for dif-
ferent values of tp, ts and hs. The plots are shown in Appendix K. The gures
show, that even for small changes in the three parameters can change the stress
distribution in the whole model. The stress distribution for the dimensions cor-
responding to the size of the dimensions of the bridge deck (see Figure K.7)
gives a plot, where the hot spots are located at the back of the vehicle. How-
ever, when the dimensions are lowered these hot spots disappear and other
hot spots appear in other places for the plate, which make it almost impossible
to make the analysis by extracting the stress using a macro. A solution could be
to split the plate and stieners into two parts and tie them together. By doing
this, the maximum stress could be found for just the plate by using a macro.
However, this implies that it doesn't matter where maximum stress is located
in the plate.
To test the algorithm and to see if the dimensions in [15] can be recovered using
the optimization program, the constrain is change to:
σHS ≥∆σR

than the stress range and will cause fatigue cracks. This analysis will only be

Chapter 8
Combined optimization
program
In chapter 7 it was shown that it is possible to make optimize programs for
the deection of a beam and stability of a stiened plate. The optimization of
fatigue was not developed properly. In this chapter it is shown how to make an
optimization program, which can optimize for two optimization problems. For
this purpose the stiened plate in section 7.2 is used, and the two optimizations
will be for stability and fatigue. Since it was not possible to optimize for fatigue,
this will only be a demonstration of have the program can be set-up to optimize
for two problems.
The FE models from section 7.2 and section 7.3 is reused together with the
dimensions, object function and input arguments.
Small changes are made
in the scripts and self-programmed functions for the names of the variables.
The scripts and self-programmed functions can be found in Appendix F. The
nonlinear constrain function will now have two constrains
λ ≥A0
A
∆σR ≥σHS
(8.1)
For this optimization program, only one analysis is performed. The initial guess
will be IG 1 in Table 7.9.
Based on the previous optimization analysis, it is expected that the results
primarily will be based on the optimization of the buckling, since the fatigue
optimization resulted in the lower bounds in section 7.3.

The results show that the optimization program is reducing the material usage
